 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right"><B>Exhibit 99 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">FOR IMMEDIATE RELEASE </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">December&nbsp;21, 2021 </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>GENERAL MILLS REPORTS FISCAL 2022 SECOND-QUARTER RESULTS </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net sales increased 6&nbsp;percent to $5.0&nbsp;billion; organic net sales<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> were up 5&nbsp;percent </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating profit declined 13&nbsp;percent to $800&nbsp;million; constant-currency adjusted operating profit
was down 6&nbsp;percent, reflecting significant input cost inflation and elevated costs related to supply chain disruptions </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted earnings per share (EPS) totaled $0.97, down 13&nbsp;percent from the prior year; adjusted diluted EPS
of $0.99 was down 7&nbsp;percent in constant currency </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Company updates full-year fiscal 2022 outlook to reflect stronger net sales growth, higher costs, and the
impact of the European Yoplait divestiture </B></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><I>&sup1;</I></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left"><I>Please see Note 7 to the Consolidated Financial Statements below for reconciliation of this and other <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures used in this release. </I></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">MINNEAPOLIS, Minn. &#150;
December&nbsp;21, 2021 &#150; General Mills (NYSE: GIS) today reported results for the second quarter ended November&nbsp;28, 2021. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;We continued to compete effectively and execute well this quarter in a challenging operating environment,&#148; said General Mills
Chairman and Chief Executive Officer Jeff Harmening. &#147;In the face of an unprecedented combination of input cost inflation and supply chain disruptions, we&#146;re moving quickly to keep our trusted brands on store shelves for consumers while
driving net price realization to protect our bottom line. As a result, we now expect to meet or exceed each of our financial targets for the year. We also advanced our portfolio reshaping efforts in the quarter, and we&#146;re more confident than
ever that General Mills will emerge from the pandemic a stronger company better geared to generate profitable growth in line with our Accelerate strategy.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">General Mills is executing its Accelerate strategy to drive sustainable, profitable growth and
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-tier</FONT> shareholder returns over the long term. The strategy focuses on four pillars to create competitive advantages and win: boldly building brands, relentlessly innovating, unleashing scale, and being a
force for good. The company is prioritizing its core markets, global platforms, and local gem brands that have the best prospects for profitable growth and is committed to reshaping its portfolio with strategic acquisitions and divestitures,
including its recent pet treats acquisition and European Yoplait divestiture, to further enhance its growth profile. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">General Mills
expects changes in consumer behaviors driven by the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19</FONT> pandemic will result in ongoing elevated consumer demand for food at home, relative to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels.
These changes include more time spent working from home and increased consumer appreciation for cooking and baking. In addition, an increase in the pet population and further humanization and premiumization of pet food during the pandemic are
expected to create tailwinds for the pet food category. The company plans to capitalize on these opportunities, addressing evolving consumer needs through its leading brands, innovation, and advantaged capabilities to generate profitable growth.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Second Quarter Results Summary </U></B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net sales</B> increased 6&nbsp;percent to $5.0&nbsp;billion, including 1 point of favorable foreign currency
exchange. Organic net sales increased 5&nbsp;percent, reflecting 5 points of positive organic net price realization and mix. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross margin</B> was down 400 basis points to 32.5&nbsp;percent of net sales, driven by higher input costs and
unfavorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> effects, partially offset by favorable net price realization and mix. Adjusted gross margin was down 330 basis points to 32.2&nbsp;percent of
net sales, driven by input cost inflation and higher other cost of goods sold, including elevated costs related to supply chain disruptions, partially offset by favorable net price realization and mix and Holistic Margin Management (HMM) cost
savings. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating profit </B>of $800&nbsp;million was down 13&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by lower gross profit
dollars and higher transaction costs and acquisition integration costs<B>. Operating profit margin</B> of 15.9&nbsp;percent was down 350 basis points. Constant-currency adjusted operating profit declined 6&nbsp;percent, driven by lower adjusted
gross profit dollars, partially offset by lower adjusted selling, general, and administrative (SG&amp;A) expenses. Adjusted operating profit margin decreased 200 basis points to 16.3&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net earnings attributable to General Mills</B> was down 13&nbsp;percent to $597&nbsp;million and <B>diluted
EPS</B> was down 13&nbsp;percent to $0.97, primarily reflecting lower operating profit. Adjusted diluted EPS of $0.99 was down 7&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by lower adjusted operating profit. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis</B>, relative to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, second-quarter results included: net sales and organic net sales up 6&nbsp;percent; operating profit down 1&nbsp;percent and adjusted operating profit flat in constant currency; and diluted EPS
and constant-currency adjusted diluted EPS each up 1&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Six Month Results Summary </U></B></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net sales</B> increased 5&nbsp;percent to $9.6&nbsp;billion, including 1 point of favorable foreign currency
exchange. Organic net sales increased 4&nbsp;percent, reflecting 4 points of positive organic net price realization and mix. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross margin</B> was down 270 basis points to 33.8&nbsp;percent of net sales, driven by higher input costs and
unfavorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> effects, partially offset by favorable net price realization and mix. Adjusted gross margin was down 250 basis points to 33.4&nbsp;percent of
net sales, driven by input cost inflation and higher other cost of goods sold, including elevated costs related to supply chain disruptions, partially offset by HMM cost savings and favorable net price realization and mix. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating profit </B>of $1.6&nbsp;billion was down 7&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by lower gross profit
dollars and higher transaction costs and acquisition integration costs.<B> Operating profit margin</B> of 17.2&nbsp;percent was down 230 basis points. Constant-currency adjusted operating profit declined 4&nbsp;percent, driven by lower adjusted
gross profit dollars, partially offset by lower adjusted SG&amp;A expenses. Adjusted operating profit margin decreased 150 basis points to 17.2&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net earnings attributable to General Mills</B> was down 8&nbsp;percent to $1.2&nbsp;billion and <B>diluted
EPS</B> was down 7&nbsp;percent to $1.99, primarily reflecting lower operating profit. Adjusted diluted EPS of $1.98 was down 4&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by lower adjusted operating profit. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis</B>, relative to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> results included: net sales and organic net sales each up 6&nbsp;percent; operating profit up 6&nbsp;percent and adjusted operating profit up
4&nbsp;percent in constant currency; diluted EPS up 5&nbsp;percent and adjusted diluted EPS up 6&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Portfolio Reshaping </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">General Mills took important
steps to further advance its portfolio reshaping efforts in the second quarter, in line with its Accelerate strategy. On November&nbsp;24, the company announced the conclusion of agreements to sell its European dough businesses to
C&eacute;r&eacute;lia. These transactions, which are expected to close by the end of fiscal 2022 subject to competition approvals, are not expected to have a material impact on adjusted diluted EPS. On November&nbsp;30, the company completed the
sale of its European Yoplait operations to Sodiaal. The company estimates the European Yoplait transaction will reduce fiscal 2022 adjusted operating profit and adjusted diluted EPS by approximately 1&nbsp;percent. With these divestitures and the
pet treats acquisition that closed in the first quarter, General Mills is increasing its focus on its faster-growing global platforms, enhancing its organic net sales growth rate, and improving its adjusted operating profit margin profile. </P>
</DIV></Center>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>North America Retail Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net sales for General Mills&#146; North America Retail segment increased 2&nbsp;percent to $2.98&nbsp;billion, driven by favorable net price
realization and mix, partially offset by lower pound volume. Organic net sales increased 1&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, relative to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT>
levels, second-quarter organic net sales were up 5&nbsp;percent. Net sales were up 16&nbsp;percent in U.S. Snacks, up 3&nbsp;percent in U.S. Cereal, and up 1&nbsp;percent in constant currency in Canada. U.S. Yogurt net sales essentially matched <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-ago</FONT> levels and U.S Meals&nbsp;&amp; Baking net sales were down 4&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit of $649&nbsp;million was down 7&nbsp;percent as reported and down 8&nbsp;percent in constant currency,
driven primarily by higher input costs and lower volume, partially offset by favorable net price realization and mix and lower SG&amp;A expenses. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, segment operating profit was
flat in constant currency. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through six months, North America Retail segment net sales were essentially in line with last year at
$5.61&nbsp;billion. Organic net sales were down 1&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half organic net sales were up 5&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit of $1.27&nbsp;billion was down
9&nbsp;percent as reported and down 10&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by higher input costs and lower volume, partially offset by favorable net price realization and mix and lower SG&amp;A expenses. On a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half segment operating profit was up 2&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Pet
Segment </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net sales for the Pet segment increased 29&nbsp;percent to $593&nbsp;million, driven by strong volume growth and favorable net
price realization and mix, including a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">15-point</FONT> net sales benefit from the pet treats acquisition, which closed on July 6. Organic net sales were up 14&nbsp;percent despite a difficult comparison to the
prior-year period that benefited from an increase in retail inventory. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, second-quarter organic net sales were up 16&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit increased
10&nbsp;percent to $132&nbsp;million, driven primarily by higher volume and favorable net price realization and mix, partially offset by higher input costs and higher SG&amp;A expenses. Profit results in the quarter included a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> inventory adjustment and other acquisition-related expenses totaling $11&nbsp;million. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, segment operating profit was up
28&nbsp;percent. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through six months, Pet segment net sales increased 27&nbsp;percent to $1.08&nbsp;billion, driven by positive
contributions from volume growth and favorable net price realization and mix. Organic net sales were up 16&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half organic net sales were up 14&nbsp;percent.
The Blue Buffalo brand drove strong <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-date</FONT></FONT> retail sales growth and market share gains in measured channels. In addition, retail sales for the recently acquired pet
treat brands were up 22&nbsp;percent in measured channels in the first half. Segment operating profit increased 18&nbsp;percent to $247&nbsp;million, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix and higher volume, partially offset by
higher input costs and higher SG&amp;A expenses. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half segment operating profit was up 24&nbsp;percent. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Convenience Stores&nbsp;&amp; Foodservice Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net sales for the Convenience Stores&nbsp;&amp; Foodservice segment increased 23&nbsp;percent to $541&nbsp;million, reflecting ongoing recovery
in key away-from-home food channels including schools, restaurants, lodging, and convenience stores, as well as market index pricing on bakery flour. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, relative to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, second-quarter organic net sales were up 3&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit increased 20&nbsp;percent to $94&nbsp;million, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and higher
volume, partially offset by higher input costs. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, segment operating profit was down 10&nbsp;percent. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through six months, Convenience Stores&nbsp;&amp; Foodservice net sales increased 23&nbsp;percent to $1.02&nbsp;billion. On a <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half organic net sales were up 3&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit increased 33&nbsp;percent to $196&nbsp;million, driven by favorable net price realization and mix and
higher volume, partially offset by higher input costs. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half segment operating profit was down 2&nbsp;percent. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Europe&nbsp;&amp; Australia Segment </U></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net
sales for the Europe&nbsp;&amp; Australia segment were down 1&nbsp;percent to $464&nbsp;million, driven primarily by lower pound volume, partially offset by positive net price realization and mix and favorable foreign currency exchange. Organic net
sales were down 2&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, relative to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, second-quarter organic net sales were flat. Net sales performance was
driven by declines on yogurt and dough. Segment operating profit totaled $16&nbsp;million compared to $36&nbsp;million a year ago, driven primarily by higher input costs and lower volume. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound
growth basis, segment operating profit was down 35&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through six months, Europe&nbsp;&amp; Australia net sales increased 2&nbsp;percent to
$981&nbsp;million, including 3 points of favorable foreign currency exchange. Organic net sales were down 1&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half organic net sales were up 2&nbsp;percent.
Segment operating profit of $61&nbsp;million was down 31&nbsp;percent as reported and down 37&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by higher input costs. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis,
first-half segment operating profit was down 4&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Asia&nbsp;&amp; Latin America Segment </U></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net sales for the Asia&nbsp;&amp; Latin America segment increased 5&nbsp;percent to $450&nbsp;million, driven by positive net price realization
and mix and favorable foreign currency exchange, partially offset by lower pound volume. Organic net sales also increased 5&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, relative to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels, second-quarter organic net sales were up 7&nbsp;percent. Net sales performance was led by <I>Yoki</I> meals and snacks in Brazil and
<I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT></I> ice cream in China. Segment operating profit of $44&nbsp;million was up 43&nbsp;percent as reported and up 40&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by favorable net price
realization and mix and lower SG&amp;A expenses. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, segment operating profit was up 23&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Through six months, Asia&nbsp;&amp; Latin America net sales increased 6&nbsp;percent to $864&nbsp;million, driven by positive net price
realization and mix and favorable foreign currency exchange, partially offset by lower pound volume. Organic net sales increased 5&nbsp;percent. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half organic net sales
were up 9&nbsp;percent. Segment operating profit of $59&nbsp;million was up 17&nbsp;percent as reported and up 14&nbsp;percent in constant currency, driven primarily by favorable net price realization and mix, partially offset by lower volume and
higher input costs. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth basis, first-half segment operating profit was up 20&nbsp;percent in constant currency. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Joint Venture Summary </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Second-quarter net sales
for Cereal Partners Worldwide (CPW) were down 2&nbsp;percent in constant currency, reflecting the comparison against elevated demand for food at home a year ago. Constant-currency net sales increased 8&nbsp;percent for
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">H&auml;agen-Dazs</FONT> Japan (HDJ), driven by strong new product performance. Combined <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> earnings from joint ventures were down 9&nbsp;percent to $33&nbsp;million,
driven by lower profit at CPW. Through six months, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> earnings from joint ventures were down 20&nbsp;percent to $62&nbsp;million. On a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth
basis, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> earnings from joint ventures were up 15&nbsp;percent in the second quarter and in the first half. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Other Income Statement Items </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Unallocated
corporate items totaled $132&nbsp;million net expense in the second quarter of fiscal 2022, compared to $48&nbsp;million net expense a year ago. Excluding <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT>
valuation effects and other items affecting comparability, unallocated corporate items totaled $112&nbsp;million net expense this year compared to $100&nbsp;million net expense last year. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring, impairment, and other exit costs totaled $2&nbsp;million in the second quarter and were an insignificant amount a year ago
<I>(please see Note 3 below for more information on these charges)</I>. <I></I> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net interest expense totaled $93&nbsp;million in the
second quarter compared to $101&nbsp;million a year ago, driven primarily by lower rates and lower average debt balances. The effective tax rate in the quarter was 21.7&nbsp;percent compared to 22.3&nbsp;percent last year <I>(please see Note 6 below
for more information on our effective tax rate)</I>. The adjusted effective tax rate of 22.3&nbsp;percent was in line with a year ago. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Cash Flow
Generation and Cash Returns </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Cash provided by operating activities increased 5&nbsp;percent to $1.50&nbsp;billion through six months of fiscal
2022, driven primarily by changes in inventories, partially offset by changes in accounts payable. Capital investments of $224&nbsp;million were down 1&nbsp;percent from a year ago. Dividends paid increased 1&nbsp;percent to $623&nbsp;million.
General Mills repurchased approximately 6.2&nbsp;million shares of common stock through six months of fiscal 2022 for a total of $375&nbsp;million. Average diluted shares outstanding decreased 1&nbsp;percent to 614&nbsp;million. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><U>Fiscal 2022 Outlook </U></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">General Mills updated its
guidance for fiscal 2022 to reflect stronger topline growth and significantly higher input costs than originally expected, as well as the impact of the European Yoplait divestiture. The company&#146;s updated full-year fiscal 2022 financial targets
are summarized below: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Organic net sales</B> are now expected to increase 4 to 5&nbsp;percent, due to stronger-than-expected
performance in the first and second quarters and incremental Strategic Revenue Management actions that will take effect in the second half. Full-year organic net sales were previously expected to be toward the higher end of the range of down 1 to
3&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">

increased guidance on organic net sales, significantly higher input costs than originally expected, and the impact of the European Yoplait divestiture, which is estimated to reduce fiscal 2022 adjusted operating profit by approximately
1&nbsp;percent. For the full year, the company now anticipates cost of goods sold headwinds will be approximately $500&nbsp;million higher than what was assumed in its initial fiscal 2022 outlook, inclusive of higher input cost inflation, which is
now expected to be 8 to 9&nbsp;percent, as well as elevated costs related to supply chain disruptions. Adjusted operating profit was previously expected to be toward the higher end of the range of down 2 to 4&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

1&nbsp;percent, driven by the same changes impacting the adjusted operating profit outlook, including an estimated 1&nbsp;percent reduction from the European Yoplait divestiture. Adjusted diluted EPS were previously expected to be toward the higher

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">General Mills will issue <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-recorded</FONT> management remarks today, December&nbsp;21, 2021, at approximately 6:30 a.m.
Central time (7:30 a.m. Eastern time) and will hold a live, webcasted question and answer session beginning at 8:00 a.m. Central time (9:00 a.m. Eastern time). The <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-recorded</FONT> remarks and the webcast will be
made available at <U>www.generalmills.com/investors</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This press release contains forward-looking statements within the meaning of the Private
Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995 that are based on our current expectations and assumptions. These forward-looking statements, including the statements under the caption &#147;Fiscal 2022 Outlook,&#148; and statements made by
Mr.&nbsp;Harmening, are subject to certain risks and uncertainties that could cause actual results to differ materially from the potential results discussed in the forward-looking statements. In particular, our predictions about future net sales and
earnings could be affected by a variety of factors, including: the impact of the coronavirus <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(COVID-19)</FONT> pandemic on our business, suppliers, consumers, customers, and employees; disruptions or inefficiencies
in the supply chain, including any impact of the coronavirus <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(COVID-19)</FONT> pandemic; competitive dynamics in the consumer foods industry and the markets for our products, including new product introductions,
advertising activities, pricing actions, and promotional activities of our competitors; economic conditions, including changes in inflation rates, interest rates, tax rates, or the availability of capital; product development and innovation;
consumer acceptance of new products and product improvements; consumer reaction to pricing actions and changes in promotion levels; acquisitions or dispositions of businesses or assets; changes in capital structure; changes in the legal and
regulatory environment, including tax legislation, labeling and advertising regulations, and litigation; impairments in the carrying value of goodwill, other intangible assets, or other long-lived assets, or changes in the useful lives of other
intangible assets; changes in accounting standards and the impact of significant accounting estimates; product quality and safety issues, including recalls and product liability; changes in consumer demand for our products; effectiveness of
advertising, marketing, and promotional programs; changes in consumer behavior, trends, and preferences, including weight loss trends; consumer perception of health-related issues, including obesity; consolidation in the retail environment; changes
in purchasing and inventory levels of significant customers; fluctuations in the cost and availability of supply chain resources, including raw materials, packaging, energy, and transportation; effectiveness of restructuring and cost saving
initiatives; volatility in the market value of derivatives used to manage price risk for certain commodities; benefit plan expenses due to changes in plan asset values and discount rates used to determine plan liabilities; failure or breach of our
information technology systems; foreign economic conditions, including currency rate fluctuations; and political unrest in foreign markets and economic uncertainty due to terrorism or war. The company undertakes no obligation to publicly revise any
forward-looking statement to reflect any future events or circumstances. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"># # # </P>

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">GENERAL MILLS, INC. AND SUBSIDIARIES </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">(Unaudited) </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(1)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">The accompanying Consolidated Financial Statements of General Mills, Inc. (we, us, our, General Mills, or the
Company) have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States for annual and interim financial information. In the opinion of management, all adjustments considered necessary for a fair presentation
have been included and are of a normal recurring nature. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(2)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">During the second quarter of fiscal 2022, we entered into definitive agreements to sell our European dough
businesses. The transactions are expected to close by the end of fiscal 2022, subject to appropriate labor consultations, regulatory approvals, and other customary closing conditions. The associated assets and liabilities have an immaterial impact
on the presentation of our Consolidated Balance Sheets of November&nbsp;28, 2021. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of fiscal
2022, we acquired the Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business for $1.2&nbsp;billion in cash. We financed the transaction with a combination of cash on hand and short-term debt. We consolidated the Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business into our
Consolidated Balance Sheets and recorded goodwill of $759&nbsp;million, indefinite-lived intangible assets for the <I>Nudges</I>, <I>Top Chews</I> and <I>True Chews</I> brands totaling $330&nbsp;million in aggregate, and a finite-lived customer
relationship asset of $40&nbsp;million. The goodwill is included in the Pet reporting unit and is deductible for tax purposes. The pro forma effects of this acquisition were not material. We have conducted a preliminary assessment of the fair value
of the acquired assets and liabilities of the Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business. The consolidated results of the Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business are reported in our Pet operating segment on a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-month</FONT> lag. Accordingly, our Consolidated Statements of Earnings include four months of operating results for the acquired business for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended
November&nbsp;28, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of fiscal 2022, we entered into a definitive agreement to sell our 51&nbsp;percent
controlling interest in Yoplait SAS, and our 50&nbsp;percent interest in Yoplait Marques SNC and Libert&eacute; Marques S&agrave;rl to Sodiaal International (Sodiaal) in exchange for full ownership of the Canadian Yoplait business, a reduced royalty
rate for the use of <I>Yoplait</I> and <I>Libert&eacute;</I> brands in the United States and Canada, and cash. The transaction closed subsequent to the end of the second quarter of fiscal 2022. We expect to record a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain on the sale of this business during the third quarter of fiscal 2022. We have classified all Yoplait SAS, Yoplait Marques SNC and Libert&eacute; Marques S&agrave;rl assets and liabilities as held
for sale in our Consolidated Balance Sheets as of November&nbsp;28, 2021. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

segment to drive efficiencies in manufacturing and logistics operations. We expect to incur approximately $21&nbsp;million of restructuring charges and project-related costs related to these actions, of which approximately $12&nbsp;million will be
cash. These charges are expected to consist of approximately $8&nbsp;million of severance and $10&nbsp;million of other costs, primarily asset write-offs. We also expect to incur approximately $3&nbsp;million of project-related costs. We recognized
$8&nbsp;million of severance and $5&nbsp;million of other costs in the second quarter of fiscal 2022. We expect this action to be completed by the end of fiscal 2024. We also recorded $10&nbsp;million of recoveries related to restructuring actions
previously announced. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

positions and grain inventories in the second quarter of fiscal 2022 compared to a $46&nbsp;million net decrease in expense in the same period last year. We recorded $10&nbsp;million of net gains related to valuation adjustments and the gain on sale
of certain corporate investments in the second quarter of fiscal 2022 compared to $6&nbsp;million of net gains related to valuation adjustments in the second quarter of fiscal 2021. In addition, we recorded $4&nbsp;million of integration costs
related to our acquisition of Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business and $38&nbsp;million of transaction costs related to the agreement to sell our 51&nbsp;percent controlling interest in Yoplait SAS and our 50&nbsp;percent interest in Yoplait
Marques SNC and Libert&eacute; Marques S&agrave;rl and the agreements to sell our European dough businesses in the second quarter of fiscal 2022. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation of certain commodity positions and grain inventories in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;28, 2021, compared to a $62&nbsp;million net
decrease in expense in the same period last year. We recorded $10&nbsp;million of net gains related to valuation adjustments and the gain on sale of certain corporate investments in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended
November&nbsp;28, 2021, compared to $19&nbsp;million of net gains related to certain corporate investment valuation adjustments in the same period last year. In addition, we recorded $16&nbsp;million of integration costs related to our acquisition
of Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business and $48&nbsp;million of transaction costs related to the agreement to sell our 51&nbsp;percent controlling interest in Yoplait SAS and our 50&nbsp;percent interest in Yoplait Marques SNC and Libert&eacute;
Marques S&agrave;rl and the agreements to sell our European dough businesses in the second quarter of fiscal 2022. In addition, we recorded a $21&nbsp;million recovery related to a Brazil indirect tax item and a $13&nbsp;million insurance recovery
in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;28, 2021. We also recorded a $7&nbsp;million charge related to a product recall in our international Green Giant business in the

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(6)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">The effective tax rate for the second quarter of fiscal 2022 was 21.7&nbsp;percent compared to
22.3&nbsp;percent for the second quarter of fiscal 2021. The 0.6 percentage point decrease was primarily due to favorable changes in earnings mix by jurisdiction in fiscal 2022, partially offset by certain nonrecurring discrete tax benefits recorded
in the second quarter of fiscal 2021. Our effective tax rate excluding certain items affecting comparability was 22.3&nbsp;percent in the quarter ended November&nbsp;28, 2021, consistent with the same period last year (see the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">&#147;Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures&#148; section below for a description of our use of measures not defined by GAAP). </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The effective tax rate for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;28, 2021, was 21.7&nbsp;percent
compared to 22.2&nbsp;percent for the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;29, 2020. The 0.5 percentage point decrease was primarily due to favorable changes in earnings mix by jurisdiction in fiscal 2022. Our
effective tax rate excluding certain items affecting comparability was 22.0&nbsp;percent in the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">six-month</FONT> period ended November&nbsp;28, 2021, compared to 22.1&nbsp;percent in the same period last year (see
the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">&#147;Non-GAAP</FONT> Measures&#148; section below for a description of our use of measures not defined by GAAP). The 0.1 percentage point decrease is primarily due to favorable changes in earnings mix by
jurisdiction in fiscal 2022, partially offset by certain nonrecurring discrete tax benefits recorded in fiscal 2021. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The United States
Congress is currently working to enact a tax reform bill, which would result in significant changes to the U.S. tax system. We expect that if a bill is enacted, it could have a material impact on our Consolidated Financial Statements in future
periods. We continue to monitor developments and assess the impact to General Mills. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">(7)</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">We have included measures in this release that are not defined by GAAP. We believe that these measures provide
useful information to investors, and include these measures in other communications to investors. For each of these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures, we are providing below a reconciliation of the differences
between the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure and the most directly comparable GAAP measure, an explanation of why we believe the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure provides useful information to
investors and any additional material purposes for which our management or Board of Directors uses the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measure. These <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures should be viewed in
addition to, and not in lieu of, the comparable GAAP measure. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We provide organic net sales growth rates for our
consolidated net sales and segment net sales. This measure is used in reporting to our Board of Directors and executive management and as a component of the Board of Directors&#146; measurement of our performance for incentive compensation purposes.
We believe that organic net sales growth rates provide useful information to investors because they provide transparency to underlying performance in our net sales by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations,
acquisitions, divestitures, and a 53rd&nbsp;fiscal week, when applicable, have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> comparability. A reconciliation of these measures to reported net sales
growth rates, the relevant GAAP measures, are included in our Operating Segment Results above. </P>
</DIV></Center>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Certain measures in this release are presented excluding the impact of foreign currency
exchange (constant-currency). To present this information, current period results for entities reporting in currencies other than United States dollars are translated into United States dollars at the average exchange rates in effect during the
corresponding period of the prior fiscal year, rather than the actual average exchange rates in effect during the current fiscal year. Therefore, the foreign currency impact is equal to current year results in local currencies multiplied by the
change in the average foreign currency exchange rate between the current fiscal period and the corresponding period of the prior fiscal year. We believe that these constant-currency measures provide useful information to investors because they
provide transparency to underlying performance by excluding the effect that foreign currency exchange rate fluctuations have on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">period-to-period</FONT></FONT> comparability given
volatility in foreign currency exchange markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Also, certain measures in this release are presented on an adjusted basis. The
adjustments are either items resulting from infrequently occurring events or items that, in management&#146;s judgment, significantly affect the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> assessment
of operating results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our fiscal 2022 outlook for organic net sales growth, adjusted operating profit growth, adjusted diluted EPS growth,
and free cash flow conversion are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude, or have otherwise been adjusted for, items impacting comparability, including the effect of foreign currency exchange rate
fluctuations, acquisitions, divestitures, and a 53rd week, when applicable. We are not able to reconcile these forward-looking <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures to their most directly comparable forward-looking GAAP
financial measure without unreasonable efforts because we are unable to predict with a reasonable degree of certainty the actual impact of changes in foreign currency exchange rates or the timing of acquisitions and divestitures throughout fiscal
2022. The unavailable information could have a significant impact on our fiscal 2022 GAAP financial results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our fiscal 2022 guidance does
not incorporate the potential impact of the European Dough divestiture that has not yet been completed. For fiscal 2022, we currently expect: foreign currency exchange rates (based on a blend of forward and forecasted rates and hedge positions) and
acquisitions and divestitures to decrease net sales by approximately 1 point; foreign currency exchange rates to have an immaterial impact on adjusted operating profit and adjusted diluted EPS growth; and restructuring charges and project-related
costs and transaction costs and acquisition integration costs to total approximately $125&nbsp;million to $175&nbsp;million. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Significant Items
Impacting Comparability </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Several measures below are presented on an adjusted basis. The adjustments are either items resulting from infrequently
occurring events or items that, in management&#146;s judgement, significantly affect the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> assessment of operating results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following are descriptions of significant items impacting comparability of our results. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> effects</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Net <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> valuation of certain commodity positions
recognized in unallocated corporate items. Please see Note 4. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-income</FONT> tax recovery</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Recovery related to a Brazil indirect tax item recorded in fiscal 2022. Please see Note 4. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Acquisition integration costs</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Integration costs resulting from the acquisition of Tyson Foods&#146; pet treats business. Please see Note 2. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Transaction costs</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Transaction costs related to the definitive agreement to sell our 51&nbsp;percent controlling interest in Yoplait SAS, and our 50&nbsp;percent
interest in Yoplait Marques SNC and Libert&eacute; Marques S&agrave;rl to Sodiaal and the definitive agreements to sell our European dough businesses in fiscal 2022. Please see Note 2. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Restructuring charges</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Restructuring charges for Asia and Latin America segment supply chain optimization actions and previously announced restructuring actions in
fiscal 2022. Restructuring charges for previously announced restructuring actions in fiscal 2021. Please see Note 3. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Investment
activity, net</U> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Valuation adjustments and the gain on sale of certain corporate investments in fiscal 2022. Valuation adjustments of
certain corporate investments in fiscal 2021. Please see Note 4. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Product recall</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Product recall costs recorded in fiscal 2021 related to our international Green Giant business. Please see Note 4. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>CPW restructuring charges</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">CPW restructuring charges related to previously announced restructuring actions. </P>

<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

<Center><DIV STYLE="width:8.5in" align="left">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><U>Organic Net Sales on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> Compound Growth Rate Basis</U> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We believe that this measure provides useful information to investors as it compares our organic net sales growth in fiscal 2022 to <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels of activity in fiscal 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Organic net sales on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT>
compound growth rate basis are calculated as follows: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

Growth Rate Basis</U> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">We believe that this measure provides useful information to investors as it compares our constant-currency segment operating profit
growth in fiscal 2022 to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-pandemic</FONT> levels of activity in fiscal 2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Our segments&#146; constant-currency
operating profit on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">2-year</FONT> compound growth rate basis are calculated as follows: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-to-year</FONT></FONT> basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Adjusted effective income tax rates are calculated as
follows: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
